    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1153210666" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1153210666" />
    <a title="Manuel Alfonseca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35970992-manuel-alfonseca"><img alt="Manuel Alfonseca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420279369p2/35970992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1153210666?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manuel Alfonseca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manuel Alfonseca" href="/user/show/35970992-manuel-alfonseca">Manuel Alfonseca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1153210666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11193173617713989499">ENGLISH: This is the fifth time I've read Lilith. I read it first over 30 years ago, and then re-read it up to four times in six years. However, this is not my favourite George MacDonald book! This special place is held by "The Princess and the Goblin".<br/><br/>Apart from the adventure itself, which is complex and full of meaning, what I liked best in Lilith was the character of the protagonist and narrator, Mr. Vane, who always takes improper decisions, because he trusts himself too much and God too lit</span>
  <span id="freeText11193173617713989499" style="display:none">ENGLISH: This is the fifth time I've read Lilith. I read it first over 30 years ago, and then re-read it up to four times in six years. However, this is not my favourite George MacDonald book! This special place is held by "The Princess and the Goblin".<br /><br />Apart from the adventure itself, which is complex and full of meaning, what I liked best in Lilith was the character of the protagonist and narrator, Mr. Vane, who always takes improper decisions, because he trusts himself too much and God too little. But then, God always makes something good out of his blunders.<br /><br />In this novel, MacDonald shows more clearly than in other books his universalist ideas, according to which everyone will end up repenting and being forgiven, not even excluding Satan, as in the following quote: "When the Shadow comes here, it will be to lie down and sleep also. His hour will come, and he knows it will." That goes against the end of "The Princess and Curdie", published 13 years before Lilith. Despite this, the description of the experience of hell by Lilith is quite convincing.<br /><br />What I liked least was the identification of Adam with Christ and of Eve with the Virgin Mary, implicit in the following quote (and other places): <i>Then at last I understood that [he] was indeed Adam, the old and the new man; and that his wife... was Eve, the mother of us all, the lady of the New Jerusalem.</i> In the doctrine of the Church there is no identification, but contrast between them.<br /><br />ESPAÑOL: Esta es la quinta vez que he leído Lilith. La leí por primera vez hace más de 30 años, y la volví a leer hasta cuatro veces en seis años. Pero este no es mi libro favorito de George MacDonald. Ese lugar tan especial lo ocupa "La princesa y el duende".<br /><br />Aparte de la aventura en sí, que es compleja y llena de sentido, lo que más me gustó de Lilith fue el carácter del protagonista y narrador, el Sr. Veleta, que siempre toma las decisiones inadecuadas porque confía demasiado en sí mismo y demasiado poco en Dios. Pero Dios siempre saca algo bueno de sus errores.<br /><br />En esta novela, MacDonald muestra más claramente que en ninguna sus ideas universalistas, según las cuales todos acabarán arrepintiéndose y siendo perdonados, sin excluir ni siquiera a Satanás, como en esta cita: "Cuando la Sombra venga aquí, será también para acostarse y dormir. Su hora llegará, y él sabe que así será". Eso va en contra del final de "La Princesa y Curdie", que se publicó 13 años antes que Lilith. Pero la descripción del infierno en la experiencia de Lilith es muy convincente.<br /><br />Lo que menos me gustó fue la identificación de Adán con Cristo y de Eva con la Virgen María, implícita en la siguiente cita (entre otras): <i>Entonces por fin entendí que [él] era en verdad Adán, el hombre viejo y el nuevo; y que su esposa... era Eva, la madre de todos nosotros, la dama de la Nueva Jerusalén.</i> En la doctrina de la Iglesia no hay identificación, sino contraposición entre ellos.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11193173617713989499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZFtO2/R/J/P5jbzEx/jrDdoMrmJdczBesxh1753IrxsK7TTWn1Y6OKrH31+MzpFFb2k140Tjh4oJr9kN1DUWfA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0DH+3SZfB6E9oSzNBmrojsfY9mfsEHcdTsKlxBej0qu+h4TQTXYaam7rT1ZNXJLGcr1t5vWAwMn0dQkmXl5rzA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2413.George_MacDonald">About George MacDonald</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2413.George_MacDonald"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1201019294p3/2413.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/2413.George_MacDonald">George MacDonald
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,682
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9519020069736047883">George MacDonald was a Scottish author, poet, and Christian minister.<br/><br/>He was educated at Aberdeen University and after a short and stormy career as a minister at Arundel, where his unorthodox views led to his dismissal, he turned to fiction as a means of earning a living. He wrote over 50 books.<br/><br/>Known particularly for his poignant fairy tales and fantasy novels, MacDonald inspired many authors, such</span>
  <span id="freeText9519020069736047883" style="display:none">George MacDonald was a Scottish author, poet, and Christian minister.<br /><br />He was educated at Aberdeen University and after a short and stormy career as a minister at Arundel, where his unorthodox views led to his dismissal, he turned to fiction as a means of earning a living. He wrote over 50 books.<br /><br />Known particularly for his poignant fairy tales and fantasy novels, MacDonald inspired many authors, such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7014283.G_K__Chesterton" title="G.K. Chesterton" rel="nofollow noopener">G.K. Chesterton</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/233593.W__H__Auden" title="W. H. Auden" rel="nofollow noopener">W. H. Auden</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/656983.J_R_R__Tolkien" title="J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">J.R.R. Tolkien</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1069006.C__S__Lewis" title="C. S. Lewis" rel="nofollow noopener">C. S. Lewis</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/106.Madeleine_L_Engle" title="Madeleine L'Engle" rel="nofollow noopener">Madeleine L'Engle</a>. Lewis wrote that he regarded MacDonald as his "master": "Picking up a copy of <i>Phantastes</i> one day at a train-station bookstall, I began to read. A few hours later," said Lewis, "I knew that I had crossed a great frontier." G. K. Chesterton cited <i>The Princess and the Goblin</i> as a book that had "made a difference to my whole existence."<br /><br />Elizabeth Yates wrote of Sir Gibbie, "It moved me the way books did when, as a child, the great gates of literature began to open and first encounters with noble thoughts and utterances were unspeakably thrilling."<br /><br />Even <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1244.Mark_Twain" title="Mark Twain" rel="nofollow noopener">Mark Twain</a>, who initially disliked MacDonald, became friends with him, and there is some evidence that Twain was influenced by MacDonald.<br /><br />For more information, please see <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_MacDonald">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_M...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9519020069736047883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
